<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background: #f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/44px-Wikipedia-logo.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/66px-Wikipedia-logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/88px-Wikipedia-logo.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200"></div></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> has an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/apple" class="extiw" title="w:apple">apple</a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/apple" class="extiw" title="w:apple">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg/220px-Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg/330px-Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg/440px-Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg 2x" data-file-width="848" data-file-height="888"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_red_delicius_flower_end.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A red apple</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/appel#Middle_English" title="appel">appel</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/%C3%A6ppel#Old_English" title="æppel">æppel</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">apple, fruit in general, ball</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-West_Germanic/applu" title="Reconstruction:Proto-West Germanic/applu">*applu</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/aplaz" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/aplaz">*aplaz</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">apple</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scots_language" class="extiw" title="w:Scots language">Scots</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sco"><a href="/wiki/aipple#Scots" title="aipple">aipple</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy"><a href="/wiki/apel#West_Frisian" title="apel">apel</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href="/wiki/appel#Dutch" title="appel">appel</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Apfel#German" title="Apfel">Apfel</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv"><a href="/wiki/%C3%A4pple#Swedish" title="äpple">äpple</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da"><a href="/wiki/%C3%A6ble#Danish" title="æble">æble</a></i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h%E2%82%82%C3%A9b%C5%8Dl" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h₂ébōl">*h₂ébōl</a></i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h%E2%82%82%C3%A9bl%CC%A5" class="mw-redirect" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h₂ébl̥">*h₂ébl̥</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">apple</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welsh_language" class="extiw" title="w:Welsh language">Welsh</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="cy"><a href="/wiki/afal#Welsh" title="afal">afal</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Irish language">Irish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ga"><a href="/wiki/%C3%BAll#Irish" language">Russian</a></span> <i class="Cyrl mention" lang="ru"><a href="/wiki/%D1%8F%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE#Russian" title="яблоко">я́блоко</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ru-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">jábloko</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, possibly <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc"><a href="/wiki/%E1%BC%84%CE%BC%CF%80%CE%B5%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%82#Ancient_Greek" title="ἄμπελος">ἄμπελος</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English" class="extiw" title="w:American English">US</a><span class="ib-comma qualifier-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_English" class="extiw" title="w:British English">UK</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">enPR</a>: <span class="AHD enPR">ăpʹ(ə)l</span>, <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ˈæp.əl/</span>, <span class="IPA">[ˈæp.ɫ̩]</span></li>
<li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r50165410">.mw-parser-output .k-player .k-attribution{visibility:hidden}</style><table class="audiotable" style="vertical-align: bottom; display:inline-block; list-style:none;line-height: 1em; border-collapse:collapse;"><tbody><tr><td class="unicode audiolink" style="padding-right:5px; padding-left: 0;">Audio (US)</td><td class="audiofile"><span class="mw-tmh-player audio" style="width:175px;"><audio id="mwe_player_0_placeholder" preload="none" width="175" style="width:175px;" data-durationhint="1" data-mwtitle="en-us-apple.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" disabled="disabled" tabindex="-1"></audio><a class="mw-tmh-play" href="/wiki/File:en-us-apple.ogg" title="Play media" role="button"><span class="mw-tmh-play-icon"></span></a><span class="mw-tmh-duration mw-tmh-label" aria-label="1 second">0:01</span></span></td><td class="audiometa" style="font-size: 80%;">(<a href="/wiki/File:en-us-apple.ogg" title="File:en-us-apple.ogg">file</a>)</td></tr></tbody></table></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">apple</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/apples#English" title="apples">apples</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A <a href="/wiki/common" title="common">common</a>, <a href="/wiki/round" title="round">round</a> <a href="/wiki/fruit" title="fruit">fruit</a> produced by the <a href="/wiki/tree" title="tree">tree</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_domestica" title="Malus domestica">Malus domestica</a></i>, cultivated in <a href="/wiki/temperate" title="temperate">temperate</a> climates. <span class="defdate">[from 9th c.]</span>
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>c. 1378</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Langland" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Langland">William Langland</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piers_Plowman" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Piers Plowman">Piers Plowman</a></i>:
<dl><dd>I prayed pieres to pulle adown an <b>apple</b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1815</b> December (indicated as <b>1816</b>),  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jane_Austen" class="extiw" title="w:Jane Austen">[Jane Austen]</a>,  chapter IX, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emma_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:Emma (novel)">Emma:<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="A Novel. In Three Volumes.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, volume I, London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Printed [by]">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> [Charles Roworth and James Moyes] for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Murray_(publishing_house)" class="extiw" title="w:John Murray (publishing house)">John Murray</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://worldcat.org/oclc/1708336">1708336</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/emmanovelinthree131aust/page/n192/mode/1up">pages 184–185</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">I have so often heard Mr. Woodhouse recommend a baked <b>apple</b>. I believe it is the only way that Mr. Woodhouse thinks the fruit thoroughly wholesome. We have <b>apple</b> dumplings, however, very often. Patty makes an excellent <b>apple</b>-dumpling.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b> October 28,  John Vallins,  “Apples of Concord”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Guardian">The Guardian</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2013/oct/28/somerset-apples-of-concord">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Close by and under cover, I watched the juicing process. <b>Apples</b> were washed, then tipped, stalks and all, into the crusher and reduced to pulp.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Any <a href="/wiki/fruit" title="fruit">fruit</a> or <a href="/wiki/vegetable" title="vegetable">vegetable</a>, or any other thing produced by a plant such as a <a href="/wiki/gall" title="gall">gall</a> or <a href="/wiki/cone" title="cone">cone</a>, especially if produced by a tree and similar to the fruit of <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_domestica" title="Malus domestica">Malus domestica</a></i>; also (with qualifying words) used to form the names of specific fruits such as <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/custard_apple#English" title="custard apple">custard apple</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/rose_apple#English" title="rose apple">rose apple</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/thorn_apple#English" title="thorn apple">thorn apple</a></i> etc. <span class="defdate">[from 9th c.]</span>
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1585</b>, Richard Eden (translating a 1555 work by Peter Martyr), <i>Decades of the New World</i>, v:
<dl><dd>Venemous <b>apples</b> wherwith they poyson theyr arrows.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1597</b>,  John Gerarde [<i>i.e.</i>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Gerard" class="extiw" title="w:John Gerard">John Gerard</a>],  “Of the Pine Tree”, in  <cite>The Herball or Generall Historie of Plantes.<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Gathered by John Gerarde of London Master in Chirvgerie.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Imprinted at London by">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> Edm[und] Bollifant, for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonham_Norton" class="extiw" title="w:Bonham Norton">Bonham and Iohn Norton</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://worldcat.org/oclc/1184595079">1184595079</a></small>, book III, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/herballorgeneral00gera_0/page/1174/mode/1up">page 1174</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">This <b>apple</b> is called in high Dutch, Zyꝛbel: in low Dutch, Pijn appel: in Engliſh, Pine apple, Clogge, and Cone. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> The whole Cone or <b>apple</b> being boiled with freſh Horehound, ſaith <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galen" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Galen">Galen</a></i>, and afterwards boyled againe with a little hony till the decoction be come to the thicknes of hony, maketh an excellent medicine for the clenſing of the chest and lungs.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1607</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Topsell" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Topsell">Edward Topsell</a>,  chapter IX, in  <cite>The Historie of Fovre-footed Beastes.<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Describing the True and Liuely Figure of Euery Beast, with a Discourse of Their Seuerall Names, Conditions, Kindes, Vertues (both Naturall and Medicinall) Countries of Their Breed, Their Loue and Hate to Mankinde, and the Wonderfull Worke of God in Their Creation, Preseruation, and Destruction. Necessary for All Diuines and Students, because the Story of Euery Beast is Amplified with Narrations out of Scriptures, Fathers, Phylosophers, Physitians, and Poets: Wherein are Declared Diuers Hyerogliphicks, Emblems, Epigrams, and Other Good Histories, Collected out of All the Volumes of Conradvs Gesner, and All Other Writers to this Present Day.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Printed by">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jaggard" class="extiw" title="w:William Jaggard">William Iaggard</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://worldcat.org/oclc/912897215">912897215</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/TheHistoryOfFourFootedBeastsAndSerpents1658/TheHistoryOfFourFootedBeasts1607/page/n361/mode/1up">page 666</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The fruite or <b>Apples</b> of Palme-trees (eſpecially ſuch as grow in ſalt grounds neare the Sea ſides, as in <i>Cyrene</i> of <i>Affrica</i>, and <i>Indea</i>, and not in <i>Egypt</i>, <i>Cyprus</i>, <i>Syria</i>, <i>Helvetia</i>, and <i>Aſsiria</i> do fatten and feed Hogges.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1658</b>, trans. Giambattista della Porta, <i>Natural Magick</i>, I.16:
<dl><dd>In Persia there grows a deadly tree, whose <b>Apples</b> are Poison, and present death.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1765</b>, Abraham Tucker, <i>The Light of Nature Pursued</i>, page 337:
<dl><dd>The fly injects her juices into the oak-leaf, to raise an <b>apple</b> for hatching her young.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1784</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Cook" class="extiw" title="w:James Cook">James Cook</a>,  <cite>A Voyage to the Pacific Ocean. Undertaken, by the Command of His Majesty, for Making Discoveries in the Northern Hemisphere.<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="To Determine the Position and Extent of the West Side of North America; its Distance from Asia; and the Practicability of a Northern Passage to Europe. Henry Roberts, under the Direction of Captain Cook; and with a Great Variety of Portraits of Persons, Views of Places, and Historical Representations of Remarkable Incidents, Drawn by Mr. [John] Webber during the Voyage, and Engraved by the Most Eminent Artists. Published by Order of the Lords Commissioners of the Admiralty.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></cite>, volume II, London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Printed by">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Strahan_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:William Strahan (publisher)">W[illiam] and A. Strahan</a>; for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Nicol_(bookseller)" class="extiw" title="w:George Nicol (bookseller)">G[eorge] Nicol</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="bookseller to His Majesty, in the Strand">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>; and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Cadell_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Cadell (publisher)">T[homas] Cadell</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="in the Strand.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://worldcat.org/oclc/1582037">1582037</a></small>, book III (Transactions at Otaheite, and the Society Islands; and Prosecution of the Voyage to the Coast of North America), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/voyagetopacifico02cook/page/174/mode/1up">page 174</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">It [Otaheite] is remarkable for producing great quantities of that delicious fruit we called <b>apples</b>, which are found in none of the others, except Eimeo.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1800</b>, John Tuke,  <i>General View of the Agriculture of the North Riding of Yorkshire</i>, page 150:
<dl><dd>It is generally thought, that the curled topped potatoe proceeds from a neglect of raising fresh sorts from the <b>apple</b> or [potato-]seed.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1825</b>, Theodric Romeyn Beck, <i>Elements of Medical Jurisprudence</i>, 2nd edition, page 565:
<dl><dd><i>Hippomane mancinella.</i> (Manchineel-tree.) Dr. Peysonnel relates that a soldier, who was a slave with the Turks, eat some of the <b>apples</b> of this tree, and was soon seized with a swelling and pain of the abdomen.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1833</b>, Charles Williams, <i>The Vegetable World</i>, page 179:
<dl><dd>One kind of <b>apple</b> or gall, inhabited only by one grub, is hard and woody on the outside, resembling a little wooden ball, of a yellowish color, but internally it is of a soft, spongy texture.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1853</b>, Mrs. S. F. Cowper, <i>Country Rambles in England, Or, Journal of a Naturalist</i>, page 172:
<dl><dd>The cross-bill will have seeds from the <b>apple</b>, or cone of the fir—the green-finch, seeds from the uplands, or door of barn, or rick-yard.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1889</b>, United States. Department of Agriculture, <i>Report of the Secretary of Agriculture</i>, page 376:
<dl><dd>The "<b>apple</b>" or gall usually forms a somewhat kidney-shaped excrescence, attached by a small base on the concave side, and varying in size from a half an inch to an inch and a half in length.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>Something which resembles the fruit of <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_domestica" title="Malus domestica">Malus domestica</a></i>, such as a <a href="/wiki/globe" title="globe">globe</a>, <a href="/wiki/ball" title="ball">ball</a>, or <a href="/wiki/breast" title="breast">breast</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1705</b>, J. S., <i>City and Country Recreation</i>, page 104:
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> shrugging up her Shoulders, to shew the tempting <b>Apples</b> of her white Breasts, Then suddainly lets them sink again, to hide them, blushing, as if this had been done by chance.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1761</b>, <i>An Universal History: From the Earliest Accounts to the Present Time</i>, page 508:
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> count-palatine of the Rhine, who shall carry the globe or imperial <b>apple</b>; and, on his left, the marquis of Brandenburg carrying the scepter.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1851</b>, Robert Bigsby, <i>Old Places Revisited; Or the Antiquarians Enthusiast</i>, page 200:
<dl><dd>The arms of Upland were a "golden <b>apple</b>," or globe, surrounded with a belt, in allusion to the monarchy.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1956</b>, Marion Hargrove, <i>The Girl He Left Behind: Or, All Quiet in the Third Platoon</i>, page 129:
<dl><dd>Andy picked up his two grenades and followed the line into the pits. The <b>apples</b> felt strangely heavy in his hands, and when he looked at them one was as ugly and lethal-looking as the other.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1975</b>, C. W. Smith, <i>Country Music</i> IX, 256:
<dl><dd>A peasant blouse that showed the tops of those lovely little <b>apples</b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2008</b>, Harald Kleinschmidt, <i>Ruling the Waves</i>, Bibliotheca Humanistica &amp; Refo
<dl><dd>Contrary to Henricus Martellus, Behaim included the tropics [on his globe...]. Evidently, there was no space for a Fourth Continent on Behaim's <b>apple</b>, although some recollection of the Catalan map seems to lie behind the shape of southern Africa.</dd></dl></li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/baseball" title="baseball">baseball</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#obsolete" title="Appendix:Glossary">obsolete</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The <a href="/wiki/ball" title="ball">ball</a> in baseball. <span class="defdate">[from 20th c.]</span></li>

<li>The <a href="/wiki/Adam%27s_apple" title="Adam's apple">Adam's apple</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1898</b>, Hugh Charles Clifford, <i>Studies in Brown Humanity: Being Scrawls and Smudges in Sepia, White, and Yellow</i>, page 99:
<dl><dd>The sweat of fear and exertion was streaming down his face and chest, and his breath came in short, tearing, hard-drawn gasps and gulps, while the <b>apple</b> in his throat leaped up and down ceaselessly <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>

<dl><dd>Elsie went away with her parents to Belgium and the convent-school on the twelfth, and as they left The Firs in the battered station cab surrounded by boxes and trunks, Willie could not speak. The <b>apple</b> in his throat rose and remained there&nbsp;<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>

<li>The <a href="/wiki/fruit" title="fruit">fruit</a> of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tree_of_Knowledge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tree of Knowledge (page does not exist)">Tree of Knowledge</a>, eaten by Adam and Eve according to post-Biblical Christian tradition; the <a href="/wiki/forbidden_fruit" title="forbidden fruit">forbidden fruit</a>. <span class="defdate">[from 11th c.]</span>
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1667</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Milton" class="extiw" title="w:John Milton">John Milton</a>,  “<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/bub_gb_F08CAAAAQAAJ/page/n279/mode/1up">Book IX</a>”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paradise_Lost" class="extiw" title="w:Paradise Lost">Paradise Lost. <li>A <a href="/wiki/tree" title="tree">tree</a> of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Malus" title="Malus">Malus</a></i>, especially one cultivated for its edible fruit; the <a href="/wiki/apple_tree" title="apple tree">apple tree</a>. <span class="defdate">[from 15th c.]</span>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Verb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">apple</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3|s|pres-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/apples#English" title="apples">apples</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/appling#English" title="appling">appling</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past|and|past|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/appled#English" title="appled">appled</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/transitive" title="transitive">transitive</a>, <a href="/wiki/intransitive" title="intransitive">intransitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To make or become apple-like.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1992</b>,  Marilyn Strathern,  <cite>Reproducing the Future</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">One might say they have to be <b>appled</b>-up; varieties are selected for marketing which have the most apple-like qualities.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2004</b>,  Gregory David Roberts,  <cite>Shantaram: A Novel</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">He glanced at me, his cheeks <b>appled</b> in the impish grin I was learning to recognise as the clever under-side of his broad and gentle smile.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2007</b>,  Claudia D. Newcorn,  <cite>Crossover: Krisalys Chronicles of Feyree</cite>, page 35:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">A large smile <b>appled</b> his full cheeks as the four sprytes eagerly served themselves from the seeds and thinly sliced fruits.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2011</b>,  Cynthia Robinson,  <cite>The Barbary Dogs</cite>, page 57:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">She smiled, and her cheeks <b>appled</b> up and her teeth were big and flat and her mouth was wide and spacious like an open invitation.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#obsolete" title="Appendix:Glossary">obsolete</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To form buds, bulbs, or fruit.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1601</b> (1634), Philemon Holland (translator), <i>Pliny</i>, II, page 98:
<dl><dd>Either they floure, or they <b>apple</b> or els be ready to bring forth fruit.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1767</b>,  James Justice,  <cite>The British gardener's calendar</cite>, page 274:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">You may now sow upon moderate hot-beds, a few of the small Salad feeds, such as White Mustard, Rape, Cresses, and Cabbage Lettuces, and you may also sow upon other hot-beds, not to be drawn until they are pretty large and well <b>appled</b>, Radishes and Turnips, observing to sow them very thin, that the plants may have room to swell and grow;</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>1796</b> (1800), Charles Marshall, <i>Gardening</i>, page 245:
<dl><dd>The cabbage turnep is of two kinds; one <b>apples</b> above ground, and the other in it.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1807</b>,  <cite>The Complete Farmer</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Other cultivators, however, advise "that the seed collected from a few turnips thus transplanted, should be preserved and sown in drills, in order to raise plants for see for the general crop, drawing out all such as are weak and improper, leaving only those that are strong and which take the lead; and that when these have <b>appled</b> or formed bulbs, to again take out such as do not appear good and perfect, as by this means turnip seed may be procured, not only of a more vigorous nature, but which is capable of vegetating with less moisture and which produces stronger and more hardy plants.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
